<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">1999 Atlantic hurricane season</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<a href="/wiki/1997_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1997 Atlantic hurricane season">1997</a>, <a href="/wiki/1998_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1998 Atlantic hurricane season">1998</a>, <b>1999</b>, <a href="/wiki/2000_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2000 Atlantic hurricane season">2000</a>, <a href="/wiki/2001_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2001 Atlantic hurricane season">2001</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>1999 Atlantic hurricane season</b> had five <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_4_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of Category 4 Atlantic hurricanes">Category 4 hurricanes</a> – the highest number recorded in a <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="Atlantic hurricane season">single season</a> in the Atlantic basin, later tied in <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005</a>. The season officially began on June 1, and ended on November 30. These dates conventionally delimit the period of each year when most <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclones</a> form in the Atlantic basin. It was a fairly active season, mostly due to a persistent <a href="/wiki/La_Ni%C3%B1a" title="La Niña">La Niña</a> that developed in the latter half of <a href="/wiki/1998_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1998 Atlantic hurricane season">1998</a>. The first storm, Arlene, formed on June 11 to the southeast of <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>. It meandered slowly for a week and caused no impact on land. Other tropical cyclones that did not affect land were Hurricane Cindy, Tropical Storm Emily, and Tropical Depression Twelve. Localized or otherwise minor damage occurred from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Bret_(1999)" title="Hurricane Bret (1999)">Hurricanes Bret</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gert_(1999)" title="Hurricane Gert (1999)">Gert</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(1999)" title="Hurricane Jose (1999)">Jose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Harvey_(1999)" title="Tropical Storm Harvey (1999)">Tropical Storms Harvey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Katrina_(1999)" title="Tropical Storm Katrina (1999)">Katrina</a>, and Tropical Depression Seven.</p>
<p>The most significant storm of the season was <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Floyd" title="Hurricane Floyd">Hurricane Floyd</a>, a strong Category 4 hurricane that caused devastating flooding along the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">East Coast of the United States</a>, especially in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>. Damage from the storm totaled approximately $6.9 billion (1999 <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">USD</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[nb 1]</a></sup> and there were at least 77 fatalities, making it the deadliest hurricane in the United States since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Agnes" title="Hurricane Agnes">Hurricane Agnes</a> in 1972. Flooding from Floyd in North Carolina followed <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dennis_(1999)" title="Hurricane Dennis (1999)">Hurricane Dennis</a>, a slow and erratic–moving storm that dropped heavy rainfall in the eastern portion of the state. Tropical Depression Eleven in October contributed to <a href="/wiki/October_1999_Mexico_floods" title="October 1999 Mexico floods">extreme flooding in Mexico</a>, which left 636 people dead and caused $491.3 million in damage, though impact could not be distinguished from the storm itself. <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irene_(1999)" title="Hurricane Irene (1999)">Hurricane Irene</a> caused extensive flooding in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, with lesser effects in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a> and North Carolina. Irene was the second–costliest storm of the season, with about $800 million in damage. <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lenny" title="Hurricane Lenny">Hurricane Lenny</a> was an unusual eastward–moving storm in the Caribbean Sea and a strong late–season storm. It caused extensive damage in the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> in the month of November. Collectively, the storms of the 1999 Atlantic hurricane season caused at least 123 fatalities and $8.58 billion in losses.</p>
<p></p>

<td align="left"><b>Actual activity</b><br/></td>

<td align="left" colspan="5">† Most recent of several such occurrences. (<a href="/wiki/List_of_Atlantic_hurricane_records#Seasonal_activity" title="List of Atlantic hurricane records">See all</a>)</td>

<p>Ahead of and during each hurricane season, various national meteorological services, scientific agencies, and noted hurricane experts issue <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_seasonal_forecasting" title="Tropical cyclone seasonal forecasting">forecasts of hurricane activity</a>. These include forecasters from the United States <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a> (NOAA)'s <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_Prediction_Center" title="Climate Prediction Center">Climate Prediction Center</a>'s, <a href="/wiki/William_M._Gray" title="William M. Gray">William M. Gray</a> and his associates at <a href="/wiki/Colorado_State_University" title="Colorado State University">Colorado State University</a> (CSU), as well as Weather Research Center (WRC) and Tropical Storm Risk (TSR), then known as TSUNAMI. The forecasts include weekly or monthly assessments of the significant factors that help determine the number of tropical storms, hurricanes, and major hurricanes within a particular year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Background_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Background-2">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gray and his team at CSU issued their initial season outlook on December 4, 1998, predicting fourteen named storms, nine hurricanes, and four major hurricanes. The three main factors for this above average season forecast cited included a continuation of abnormally warm <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">sea surface temperatures</a>, the probability that <a href="/wiki/La_Ni%C3%B1a" title="La Niña">La Niña</a> conditions would remain, and that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quasi-Biennial_Oscillation" title="Quasi-Biennial Oscillation">Quasi-Biennial Oscillation</a> (QBO) winds would be in a westerly phase.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deccsu_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-deccsu-7">[6]</a></sup> Early in 1999, WRC issued its forecast for the season, projecting ten named storms and six hurricanes, but no prediction on the number of major hurricanes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wrc_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-wrc-5">[4]</a></sup> In subsequent outlooks from Gray and his associates in April, June, and August, the predictions were unchanged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-verification_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-verification-4">[3]</a></sup> On April 7, CSU noted that the probability of a major hurricane landfall in the United States was 72%, including a 54% chance on the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">East Coast</a> and a 40% likelihood on the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="Gulf Coast of the United States">Gulf Coast</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup> In their outlook on May 27, experts at NOAA noted that an above average season was a strong possibility. An addition to a La Niña, vertical <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> would be decreased across much of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> and tropical <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, and a favorable jet pattern for <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical waves</a> to develop into tropical cyclones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-noaamay_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-noaamay-9">[8]</a></sup> On June 1, TSR predicted that there would be 12 named storms, 7 hurricanes, and 2 major hurricanes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tsr_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-tsr-6">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>As stated by NOAA and CSU, an average Atlantic hurricane season between 1981–2010 contains roughly 12 tropical storms, 6 hurricanes, 3 major hurricanes, and an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accumulated_Cyclone_Energy" title="Accumulated Cyclone Energy">Accumulated Cyclone Energy</a> (ACE) Index of 66–103 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Background_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-Background-2">[1]</a></sup> NOAA typically categorizes a season as either above-average, average, of below-average based on the cumulative ACE Index; however, the number of tropical storms, hurricanes, and major hurricanes within a hurricane season is considered occasionally as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gray_Dec_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gray_Dec-10">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_activity">Season activity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Season activity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<center>
<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map id="timeline_575b5db08e1eb1cf4d8c77478239353e" name="timeline_575b5db08e1eb1cf4d8c77478239353e">

<area alt="October 1999 Mexico floods" coords="462,55,564,76" href="/wiki/October_1999_Mexico_floods" shape="rect" title="October 1999 Mexico floods"/>
<area alt="Tropical Storm Harvey (1999)" coords="412,40,514,61" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Harvey_(1999)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Harvey (1999)"/>

<area alt="Hurricane Floyd" coords="394,10,491,31" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Floyd" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Floyd"/>

<area alt="Hurricane Bret" coords="312,40,403,61" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Bret" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Bret"/>

</center>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Floyd_Gert_09-13-1999_1415Z.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2972" data-file-width="4875" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Floyd_Gert_09-13-1999_1415Z.png/220px-Floyd_Gert_09-13-1999_1415Z.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Floyd_Gert_09-13-1999_1415Z.png/330px-Floyd_Gert_09-13-1999_1415Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Floyd_Gert_09-13-1999_1415Z.png/440px-Floyd_Gert_09-13-1999_1415Z.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Floyd_Gert_09-13-1999_1415Z.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hurricanes Floyd and Gert pictured on September 13</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Atlantic hurricane season officially began on June 1, 1999,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-noaamay_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-noaamay-9">[8]</a></sup> and the first tropical cyclone developed on June 11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atcr_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-atcr-11">[10]</a></sup> It was an above–average season in which 16 tropical cyclones formed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mwr_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-mwr-12">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TD2TCR_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-TD2TCR-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7tcr_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-7tcr-14">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12tcr_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-12tcr-15">[14]</a></sup> Twelve depressions attained tropical storm status, and eight of these became hurricanes. Five hurricanes intensified further into major hurricanes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mwr_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-mwr-12">[11]</a></sup> The season featured a record-breaking five Category 4 hurricanes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> later tied in <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mwr2005_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-mwr2005-17">[16]</a></sup> These were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Bret_(1999)" title="Hurricane Bret (1999)">Bret</a>, Cindy, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Floyd" title="Hurricane Floyd">Floyd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gert_(1999)" title="Hurricane Gert (1999)">Gert</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lenny" title="Hurricane Lenny">Hurricane Lenny</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mwr_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-mwr-12">[11]</a></sup> The last storm of the season, Hurricane Lenny, dissipated on November 23,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ltcr_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-ltcr-18">[17]</a></sup> which was about a week before the official season ending on November 30, 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-noaamay_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-noaamay-9">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>A persistent <a href="/wiki/La_Ni%C3%B1a" title="La Niña">La Niña</a> that developed during <a href="/wiki/1998_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1998 Atlantic hurricane season">the previous season</a> was attributed to the above average activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> Between August and October, there was very low <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> over the Caribbean Sea and western Atlantic Ocean, attributed to a combination of abnormal upper-level easterly winds and low-level westerly winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> Six hurricanes and two tropical storms made landfall during the season and caused at least 123 deaths and approximately $8.58 billion in damage. Hurricane Gert also caused damage and fatalities, despite not making landfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Overall, the season's activity was reflected with a cumulative <a href="/wiki/Accumulated_cyclone_energy" title="Accumulated cyclone energy">accumulated cyclone energy</a> (ACE) rating of 177.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> ACE is, broadly speaking, a measure of the power of the hurricane multiplied by the length of time it existed, so storms that last a long time, as well as particularly strong hurricanes, have high ACEs. It is only calculated for full advisories on tropical systems at or exceeding 34 <a href="/wiki/Knot_(unit)" title="Knot (unit)">knots</a> (39 mph, 63 km/h) or tropical storm strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Systems">Systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="Timeline of the 1999 Atlantic hurricane season">Timeline of the 1999 Atlantic hurricane season</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Arlene">Tropical Storm Arlene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Arlene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arlene_06-13-1999_1215Z.png"><img alt="Arlene 06-13-1999 1215Z.png" data-file-height="1314" data-file-width="1118" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Arlene_06-13-1999_1215Z.png/150px-Arlene_06-13-1999_1215Z.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Arlene_06-13-1999_1215Z.png/225px-Arlene_06-13-1999_1215Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Arlene_06-13-1999_1215Z.png/300px-Arlene_06-13-1999_1215Z.png 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arlene_1999_track.png"><img alt="Arlene 1999 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Arlene_1999_track.png/150px-Arlene_1999_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Arlene_1999_track.png/225px-Arlene_1999_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Arlene_1999_track.png/300px-Arlene_1999_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>June 11 – June 18</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>60 mph (95 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1006 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Along a diffuse front, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_pressure_area" title="Low pressure area">broad area of low pressure</a> in association with an <a href="/wiki/Cold-core_low" title="Cold-core low">upper-level low</a> was noted several hundred miles northeast of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> on June 8. After the circulation reformed within the area of stronger <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Convection_(meteorology)" title="Convection (meteorology)">convection</a>, the NHC estimated that Tropical Depression One developed at 18:00 UTC on June 11 about 535 mi (860 km) southeast of <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>. Initially, the system resembled a <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_cyclone" title="Subtropical cyclone">subtropical cyclone</a>, due to its frontal characteristics. The nascent depression drifted northward for 24 hours, and during this time, it strengthened and was upgraded to Tropical Storm Arlene at 12:00 UTC on June 12, based on <a href="/wiki/Dvorak_technique" title="Dvorak technique">Dvorak</a> satellite classifications. The storm intensified further to its peak intensity at 00:00 UTC on June 13, with estimated <a href="/wiki/Maximum_sustained_wind" title="Maximum sustained wind">maximum sustained winds</a> of 60 mph (95 km/h) and a minimum <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barometric_pressure" title="Barometric pressure">barometric pressure</a> of 1,006 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (29.7 <a href="/wiki/Inch_of_mercury" title="Inch of mercury">inHg</a>), based on ship reports and satellite. Subsequently, weakening due to westerly wind shear, Arlene tracking westward on June 13 and turned northwest the following day. Because the steering current became poorly defined, it drifted starting on June 15, and executed a small cyclonic loop later that day. At 00:00 UTC on June 17, Arlene was downgraded to a tropical depression. Later that day, it passed about 115 mi (185 km) east of Bermuda,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atcr_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-atcr-11">[10]</a></sup> where gale-force winds and abnormally high tides were observed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> The depression weakened further due to decreasing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperatures" title="Sea surface temperatures">sea surface temperatures</a> and dissipated early on June 18.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atcr_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-atcr-11">[10]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Two">Tropical Depression Two</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Two">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tropical_Depression_Two1999.jpg"><img alt="Tropical Depression Two1999.jpg" data-file-height="1572" data-file-width="1564" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Tropical_Depression_Two1999.jpg/150px-Tropical_Depression_Two1999.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Tropical_Depression_Two1999.jpg/225px-Tropical_Depression_Two1999.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Tropical_Depression_Two1999.jpg/300px-Tropical_Depression_Two1999.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2-L_1999_track.png"><img alt="2-L 1999 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/2-L_1999_track.png/150px-2-L_1999_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/2-L_1999_track.png/225px-2-L_1999_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/2-L_1999_track.png/300px-2-L_1999_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 2 – July 3</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>35 mph (55 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1004 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> crossed the west coast of Africa on June 20. As the wave moved into the western Caribbean Sea on June 30, a broad cyclonic turning was noted. The system moved over the Yucatán Peninsula on July 1, a day before emerging into the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Campeche" title="Bay of Campeche">Bay of Campeche</a> as a weak low pressure area. Later on July 2, deep convection became more organized while the system was centered over the southwestern <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>. By 18:00 UTC, the low developed into Tropical Depression Two. Around 04:00 UTC on July 3, the depression made <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a> about 40 mi (65 km) south-southeast of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tuxpan,_Veracruz" title="Tuxpan, Veracruz">Tuxpan, Veracruz</a>, with winds of 35 mph (55 km/h). Eight hours later, it dissipated over the mountains of Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TD2TCR_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-TD2TCR-13">[12]</a></sup> The depression dropped heavy rain on the area amounting to a maximum of 20.37 in (517 mm) at Tanzabaca, San Luis Potosí.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPCMAX_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-WPCMAX-25">[24]</a></sup> In some areas, up to 12.49 in (317 mm) of precipitation fell in 24 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TD2TCR_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-TD2TCR-13">[12]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Bret">Hurricane Bret</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Hurricane Bret">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bret_08-22-1999_1431Z.png"><img alt="Bret 08-22-1999 1431Z.png" data-file-height="1475" data-file-width="1313" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Bret_08-22-1999_1431Z.png/150px-Bret_08-22-1999_1431Z.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Bret_08-22-1999_1431Z.png/225px-Bret_08-22-1999_1431Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Bret_08-22-1999_1431Z.png/300px-Bret_08-22-1999_1431Z.png 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bret_1999_track.png"><img alt="Bret 1999 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Bret_1999_track.png/150px-Bret_1999_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Bret_1999_track.png/225px-Bret_1999_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Bret_1999_track.png/300px-Bret_1999_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 18 – August 25</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>145 mph (230 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  944 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Bret" title="Hurricane Bret">Hurricane Bret</a></div>
<p>Late on August 18, a tropical wave in the Bay of Campeche spawned Tropical Depression Three. The depression drifted and was initially hampered by wind shear. By late on August 19, the depression was upgraded to Tropical Storm Bret amid more favorable atmosphere conditions. Bret then moved generally northward and strengthened into a hurricane early on August 21. Bret strengthened significantly over the next 36 hours, peaking as a 145 mph (230 km/h) Category 4 hurricane with a minimum barometric pressure of 944 mbar (27.9 inHg) on August 22. Thereafter, the storm began to weaken while curving west-northwestward. At 00:00 UTC on August 23, Bret made landfall in central <a href="/wiki/Padre_Island" title="Padre Island">Padre Island</a>, Texas, as a Category 3 hurricane with winds of 115 mph (185 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bret_TCR_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bret_TCR-26">[25]</a></sup> After moving inland, the storm weakened quickly, falling to tropical depression status on August 24. Early the following day, Bret dissipated near the border of <a href="/wiki/Coahuila" title="Coahuila">Coahuila</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chihuahua_(state)" title="Chihuahua (state)">Chihuahua</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bret_TCR_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bret_TCR-26">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bret was a small tropical cyclone that made landfall in a sparsely–populated region of Texas, resulting in relatively little damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bret_TCR_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-Bret_TCR-26">[25]</a></sup> Heavy rainfall in the area peaked at 13.18 in (335 mm) in <a href="/wiki/Sarita,_Texas" title="Sarita, Texas">Sarita</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPCMAX_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-WPCMAX-25">[24]</a></sup> At least 200 homes and large agricultural fields were flooded in <a href="/wiki/Duval_County,_Texas" title="Duval County, Texas">Duval County</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd8_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd8-27">[26]</a></sup> Strong winds left approximately 64,000 people without electricity in <a href="/wiki/South_Texas" title="South Texas">South Texas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> Four people died after a truck and a tractor collided near <a href="/wiki/Laredo,_Texas" title="Laredo, Texas">Laredo</a> due to slick roads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> In Mexico, the storm brought flooding to <a href="/wiki/Coahuila" title="Coahuila">Coahuila</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuevo_Leon" title="Nuevo Leon">Nuevo Leon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tamaulipas" title="Tamaulipas">Tamaulipas</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> with an estimated 14 in (360 mm) of rain falling in Nuevo Leon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bret_TCR_26-3"><a href="#cite_note-Bret_TCR-26">[25]</a></sup> Numerous homes in the affected regions were damaged or destroyed, leaving roughly 150 people homeless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> Three people died in Mexico – one was tramped to death during evacuation, another was electrocuted, and the third drowned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MexDeaths1_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-MexDeaths1-32">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> Overall, the storm caused $15 million in damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TXRPT_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-TXRPT-34">[33]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Cindy">Hurricane Cindy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Hurricane Cindy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cindy_08-28-1999_1245Z.png"><img alt="Cindy 08-28-1999 1245Z.png" data-file-height="1868" data-file-width="1754" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Cindy_08-28-1999_1245Z.png/150px-Cindy_08-28-1999_1245Z.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Cindy_08-28-1999_1245Z.png/225px-Cindy_08-28-1999_1245Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Cindy_08-28-1999_1245Z.png/300px-Cindy_08-28-1999_1245Z.png 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cindy_1999_track.png"><img alt="Cindy 1999 track.png" data-file-height="762" data-file-width="1024" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Cindy_1999_track.png/150px-Cindy_1999_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Cindy_1999_track.png/225px-Cindy_1999_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Cindy_1999_track.png/300px-Cindy_1999_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 19 – August 31</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>140 mph (220 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  942 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On August 18, a tropical wave moved westward off the coast of Africa. With low pressures and gradually organizing convection, Tropical Depression Four developed west of <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> early on August 19.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ctcr_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-ctcr-35">[34]</a></sup> Initially it failed to intensify due to wind shear,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ctcr_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-ctcr-35">[34]</a></sup> and the center became ill-defined on August 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc4_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc4-36">[35]</a></sup> After passing south of Cape Verde,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc5_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc5-37">[36]</a></sup> the depression intensified into Tropical Storm Cindy as the convection became concentrated around the center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc7_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc7-38">[37]</a></sup> Due to a strong ridge, Cindy moved westward, before turning northwestward by August 21.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc9_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc9-39">[38]</a></sup> Banding features gradually increased as outflow improved,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc10_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc10-40">[39]</a></sup> and late on August 21, Cindy became a hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc13_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc13-41">[40]</a></sup> Afterward, increased wind shear dislocated the convection from the center,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc14_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc14-42">[41]</a></sup> which weakened Cindy to a tropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc16_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc16-43">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>By August 23, high wind shear remained, and the storm's winds decreased to 60 mph (100 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc17_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc17-44">[43]</a></sup> The shear decreased on August 24,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ctcr_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-ctcr-35">[34]</a></sup> and the convection increased over the center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc25_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc25-45">[44]</a></sup> By late on August 25, Cindy regained hurricane status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ctcr_35-3"><a href="#cite_note-ctcr-35">[34]</a></sup> A ragged eye appeared on satellite imagery on August 27,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc21_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc21-46">[45]</a></sup> and early the next day it attained major hurricane status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc22_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc22-47">[46]</a></sup> Cindy turned north-northwestward, now showing a well-defined <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ctcr_35-4"><a href="#cite_note-ctcr-35">[34]</a></sup> and reached Category 4 intensity with winds of 140 mph (220 km/h) on August 28.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc24_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc24-48">[47]</a></sup> Turning northward, the storm remained at peak intensity until August 30, when prominent wind shear weakened Cindy again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ctcr_35-5"><a href="#cite_note-ctcr-35">[34]</a></sup> On August 31, Cindy was downgraded to a tropical storm,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disc26_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-disc26-49">[48]</a></sup> and later that day it merged with a large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extratropical_storm" title="Extratropical storm">extratropical storm</a> northwest of the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ctcr_35-6"><a href="#cite_note-ctcr-35">[34]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Dennis">Hurricane Dennis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Hurricane Dennis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Dennis_(1999)_GOES_2.PNG"><img alt="Hurricane Dennis (1999) GOES 2.PNG" data-file-height="1165" data-file-width="1437" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Hurricane_Dennis_%281999%29_GOES_2.PNG/150px-Hurricane_Dennis_%281999%29_GOES_2.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Hurricane_Dennis_%281999%29_GOES_2.PNG/225px-Hurricane_Dennis_%281999%29_GOES_2.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Hurricane_Dennis_%281999%29_GOES_2.PNG/300px-Hurricane_Dennis_%281999%29_GOES_2.PNG 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dennis_1999_track.png"><img alt="Dennis 1999 track.png" data-file-height="710" data-file-width="1024" height="104" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Dennis_1999_track.png/150px-Dennis_1999_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Dennis_1999_track.png/225px-Dennis_1999_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Dennis_1999_track.png/300px-Dennis_1999_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 24 – September 7</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>105 mph (165 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  962 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dennis_(1999)" title="Hurricane Dennis (1999)">Hurricane Dennis (1999)</a></div>
<p>Tropical Depression Five developed from a tropical wave about 220 mi (355 km) east of the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks Islands</a> on August 23. On the following day, the depression strengthened into Tropical Storm Dennis despite unfavorable westerly shear, which became a hurricane by August 26. After striking the <a href="/wiki/Abaco_Islands" title="Abaco Islands">Abaco Islands</a> in the Bahama, conditions improved, allowing for Dennis to strengthen into a Category 2 by August 28. Around this time, Dennis began to move parallel to the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_United_States" title="Southeastern United States">Southeastern United States</a>. Early on August 30, the storm peaked with maximum sustained winds of 105 mph (165 km/h) and a minimum barometric pressure of 962 mbar (28.4 inHg). By the following day, steering currents collapsed and the storm interacted with a cold front, causing Dennis to move erratically offshore North Carolina. Wind shear and cold air associated with the front weakened Dennis to a tropical storm on September 1 and removed some of its tropical characteristics. Eventually, warmer ocean temperatures caused some re-strengthening. By September 4, Dennis turned northwestward and made landfall in <a href="/wiki/Cape_Lookout_(North_Carolina)" title="Cape Lookout (North Carolina)">Cape Lookout</a>, North Carolina, as a strong tropical storm. The storm slowly weakened inland, before transitioning into an extratropical cyclone over western <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a> on September 7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dennis_TCR_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dennis_TCR-50">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the Bahamas, Dennis produced moderate winds, rain, and storm surge on <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador_Island" title="San Salvador Island">San Salvador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crooked_Island,_Bahamas" title="Crooked Island, Bahamas">Crooked Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eleuthera" title="Eleuthera">Eleuthera</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Abaco_Islands" title="Abaco Islands">Abaco Islands</a>, resulting in damage to roofs and coastal properties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> Dennis brought 6–8 ft (1.8–2.4 m) waves to the east coast of Florida, causing minor erosion and four drowning deaths. The waves left severe erosion and coastal flooding along the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Banks" title="Outer Banks">Outer Banks</a> of North Carolina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dennis_TCR_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dennis_TCR-50">[49]</a></sup> An 8 ft (2.4 m) deep channel created along <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Highway_12" title="North Carolina Highway 12">Highway 12</a> isolated three towns on <a href="/wiki/Hatteras_Island" title="Hatteras Island">Hatteras Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-isolatedtowns_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-isolatedtowns-52">[51]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Carteret_County,_North_Carolina" title="Carteret County, North Carolina">Carteret</a>, <a href="/wiki/Craven_County,_North_Carolina" title="Craven County, North Carolina">Craven</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dare_County,_North_Carolina" title="Dare County, North Carolina">Dare</a> counties, the storm damaged at least 2,025 homes and businesses to some degree.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> Heavy rainfall, peaking at 19.91 in (506 mm) at <a href="/wiki/Ocracoke,_North_Carolina" title="Ocracoke, North Carolina">Ocracoke</a>, fell in eastern North Carolina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPCMAX_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-WPCMAX-25">[24]</a></sup> Although the precipitation was generally beneficial due to drought conditions, it also damaged crops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dennis_TCR_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-Dennis_TCR-50">[49]</a></sup> Two indirect deaths occurred in <a href="/wiki/Richlands,_North_Carolina" title="Richlands, North Carolina">Richlands</a> during a weather-related car accident.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> Similar inland flooding occurred in northern and eastern Virginia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dennis_TCR_50-3"><a href="#cite_note-Dennis_TCR-50">[49]</a></sup> with precipitation reaching 10.21 in (259 mm) near <a href="/wiki/Lawrenceville,_Virginia" title="Lawrenceville, Virginia">Lawrenceville</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mid_Atl_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mid_Atl-55">[54]</a></sup> A tornado in <a href="/wiki/Hampton,_Virginia" title="Hampton, Virginia">Hampton</a> severely damaged five apartment complexes, three of which were condemned completely, as well an assisted living facility; about 460 people were forced to evacuate from the buildings, and as many as 800 vehicles may have been damaged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd9_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd9-56">[55]</a></sup> Overall damage in North Carolina and Virginia totaled about $157 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dennis_TCR_50-4"><a href="#cite_note-Dennis_TCR-50">[49]</a></sup> Generally minor flooding occurred in the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_states" title="Mid-Atlantic states">Mid-Atlantic</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd9_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-sd9-56">[55]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Emily">Tropical Storm Emily</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Emily">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emily_08-25-1999_1715Z.png"><img alt="Emily 08-25-1999 1715Z.png" data-file-height="1443" data-file-width="1359" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Emily_08-25-1999_1715Z.png/150px-Emily_08-25-1999_1715Z.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Emily_08-25-1999_1715Z.png/225px-Emily_08-25-1999_1715Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Emily_08-25-1999_1715Z.png/300px-Emily_08-25-1999_1715Z.png 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emily_1999_track.png"><img alt="Emily 1999 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Emily_1999_track.png/150px-Emily_1999_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Emily_1999_track.png/225px-Emily_1999_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Emily_1999_track.png/300px-Emily_1999_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 24 – August 28</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>50 mph (85 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1004 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical wave ahead of Hurricane Cindy exited the west coast of Africa on August 15. Minimal <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclogenesis" title="Tropical cyclogenesis">development</a> occurred initially, although the structure gradually organized as it approached the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a>. By 06:00 UTC on August 24, the NHC estimated that a tropical depression developed about 470 mi (760 km) east-northeast of <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a>. The depression strengthened into Tropical Storm Emily six hours later. At 1800 UTC on August 24, Emily attained its peak intensity with maximum sustained winds of 50 mph (85 km/h) and a minimum barometric pressure of 1,004 mbar (29.6 inHg).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etcr_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-etcr-57">[56]</a></sup> The NHC did not initiate advisories until 2100 UTC, when a <a href="/wiki/Reconnaissance_aircraft" title="Reconnaissance aircraft">reconnaissance aircraft</a> observed winds of 63 mph (101 km/h) in association with the small circulation of Emily. The agency initially predicted that the storm would intensify into a hurricane near the Windward Islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> Increased wind shear generated by Hurricane Cindy caused Emily to weaken slightly on August 25. Emily began moving slowly northwestward and progressively became more influenced by Cindy, developing occasional convective bursts. Later on August 26, the movement turned northward, well offshore the Lesser Antilles. Eventually, the storm no longer produced convective bursts, and by 12:00 UTC on August 28, Emily weakened to a tropical depression. Six hours later, the storm <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Binary_interaction" title="Binary interaction">was absorbed into Cindy</a> northeast of the Leeward Islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etcr_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-etcr-57">[56]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Seven">Tropical Depression Seven</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Seven">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tropical_Depession_Seven_06_sept_1999_1315Z.jpg"><img alt="Tropical Depession Seven 06 sept 1999 1315Z.jpg" data-file-height="1588" data-file-width="1447" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Tropical_Depession_Seven_06_sept_1999_1315Z.jpg/150px-Tropical_Depession_Seven_06_sept_1999_1315Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Tropical_Depession_Seven_06_sept_1999_1315Z.jpg/225px-Tropical_Depession_Seven_06_sept_1999_1315Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Tropical_Depession_Seven_06_sept_1999_1315Z.jpg/300px-Tropical_Depession_Seven_06_sept_1999_1315Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:7-L_1999_track.png"><img alt="7-L 1999 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/7-L_1999_track.png/150px-7-L_1999_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/7-L_1999_track.png/225px-7-L_1999_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/7-L_1999_track.png/300px-7-L_1999_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 5 – September 7</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>35 mph (55 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1006 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Interaction between a strong monsoon-type flow and a tropical wave in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Campeche" title="Bay of Campeche">Bay of Campeche</a> resulted in the development of Tropical Depression Seven on September 5. By 00:00 UTC on September 6, the depression attained maximum sustained winds of 35 mph (55 km/h) and a minimum barometric pressure of 1,006 mbar (29.7 inHg).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7tcr_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-7tcr-14">[13]</a></sup> Shortly thereafter, the center of circulation of the depression became difficult to locate, but was likely heading north-northwestward. Due to warm ocean temperatures, the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_forecast_model" title="Tropical cyclone forecast model">SHIPS model</a> predicted further intensification, despite the storm having almost no deep convection and being close to land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>At 12:00 UTC on September 6, the depression made landfall near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Pesca,_Tamaulipas" title="La Pesca, Tamaulipas">La Pesca, Tamaulipas</a>, with winds of 35 mph (55 km/h). The depression quickly weakened inland, and dissipated about twenty-four hours after landfall. Due to forecasts that the depression would strengthen to a tropical storm, the government of Mexico issued a tropical storm warning for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tampico,_Tamaulipas" title="Tampico, Tamaulipas">Tampico</a> to <a href="/wiki/Matamoros,_Tamaulipas" title="Matamoros, Tamaulipas">Matamoros, Tamaulipas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7tcr_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-7tcr-14">[13]</a></sup> The storm caused heavy rainfall in Mexico, with as much as 17.43 in (443 mm) falling in <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Mante" title="Ciudad Mante">Ciudad Mante</a> in the state of Tamaulipas. In Texas, the depression produced light rainfall, peaking at 3.35 in (85 mm) in <a href="/wiki/Harlingen,_Texas" title="Harlingen, Texas">Harlingen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Floyd">Hurricane Floyd</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Hurricane Floyd">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Floyd_09-13-1999_1415Z.png"><img alt="Floyd 09-13-1999 1415Z.png" data-file-height="2338" data-file-width="2136" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Floyd_09-13-1999_1415Z.png/150px-Floyd_09-13-1999_1415Z.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Floyd_09-13-1999_1415Z.png/225px-Floyd_09-13-1999_1415Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Floyd_09-13-1999_1415Z.png/300px-Floyd_09-13-1999_1415Z.png 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Floyd_1999_track.png"><img alt="Floyd 1999 track.png" data-file-height="1022" data-file-width="1024" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Floyd_1999_track.png/150px-Floyd_1999_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Floyd_1999_track.png/225px-Floyd_1999_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Floyd_1999_track.png/300px-Floyd_1999_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 7 – September 17</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>155 mph (250 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  921 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Floyd" title="Hurricane Floyd">Hurricane Floyd</a></div>
<p>A westward moving tropical wave developed into a tropical depression while located about 1,000 mi (1,600 km) east of the Lesser Antilles on September 7. The depression strengthened and was upgraded to Tropical Storm Floyd on the following day. Floyd became a hurricane on September 10, while curving northwestward, before the storm resumed its initial west-northwestward course late on the following day. Significant intensification occurred on September 12 and September 13. At 12:00 UTC on the latter date, Floyd peaked with maximum sustained winds of 155 mph (250 km/h) and a minimum barometric pressure of 921 mbar (27.2 inHg). Thereafter, the storm began weakening while approaching the Bahamas, decreasing to Category 3 intensity at 06:00 UTC on September 14. Six hours later, Floyd made landfall near <a href="/wiki/Alice_Town" title="Alice Town">Alice Town</a> on Eleuthera with winds of 120 mph (195 km/h), around the time that the cyclone began moving north-northwestward. Shortly before striking the Abaco Islands at 19:00 UTC, the hurricane re-intensified into a Category 4 hurricane. Early on September 15, Floyd weakened to a Category 3 hurricane and passed 110 mi (180 km) offshore Florida. Floyd weakened to a Category 2 hurricane late on September 15, while re-curving to the north-northeast. At 16:30 UTC on September 16, Floyd made landfall near <a href="/wiki/Cape_Fear_(headland)" title="Cape Fear (headland)">Cape Fear</a>, North Carolina, with winds of 105 mph (170 km/h). Thereafter, the storm rapidly weakened and was a tropical storm by early on the following day. Floyd moved along the coasts of the <a href="/wiki/Delmarva_Peninsula" title="Delmarva Peninsula">Delmarva Peninsula</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, before striking Long Island in New York early on September 17. Shortly thereafter, Floyd transitioned into an extratropical cyclone while interacting with a frontal zone over <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-floyd_tcr_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-floyd_tcr-61">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the Bahamas, a combination of strong winds and storm surge destroyed numerous restaurants, hotels, shops, and homes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup> and left tens of thousands without water, electricity, and food. One death was reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baha_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-baha-63">[62]</a></sup> Although millions of people in Florida evacuated, damage was relatively minor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-floyd_tcr_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-floyd_tcr-61">[60]</a></sup> The outerbands of Floyd produced up to 3.2 in (81 mm) of rain and tropical storm force winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Florida_Rain_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Florida_Rain-64">[63]</a></sup> As a result, hundreds of trees were downed, which damaged at 467 houses, and several hotels and businesses. Impact in <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a> was minor. North Carolina bore the brunt of the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-floyd_tcr_61-2"><a href="#cite_note-floyd_tcr-61">[60]</a></sup> Heavy precipitation fell in the eastern portion of the state, peaking at 24.06 in (611 mm) near <a href="/wiki/Southport,_North_Carolina" title="Southport, North Carolina">Southport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPCMAX_25-3"><a href="#cite_note-WPCMAX-25">[24]</a></sup> Numerous rivers experienced at least 500-year floods, causing extensive flooding. About 7,000 homes were destroyed and an additional 56,000 suffered damage, of which 17,000 houses were left uninhabitable. At the height of the storm, more than 500,000 people lacked electricity. Thirty-five fatalities and about $4 billion in damage occurred in North Carolina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cw_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-cw-65">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Flooding in Virginia damaged about 182 businesses and 9,250 houses, and left about 12 ft (3.7 m) of standing water in <a href="/wiki/Franklin,_Virginia" title="Franklin, Virginia">Franklin</a>. There were three deaths and $101 million in losses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vahurricanes_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-vahurricanes-66">[65]</a></sup> In Maryland, flooding damaged at least 694 homes, impacted numerous bridges and roads, and left over 250,000 residents without power. Similar effects occurred in <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a>, with at least 171 houses damaged and numerous roads being inundated or washed out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd9_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-sd9-56">[55]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, flash flooding affected over 10,000 homes and left more than 500,000 people without electricity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cw_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-cw-65">[64]</a></sup> Losses reached $60 million and there were 13 deaths in the state. The storm also caused significant impact in New Jersey, where 3,978 homes, 1,358 apartments, and 1,758 businesses were destroyed or suffer major damage. Six deaths occurred in the state. <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd9_56-3"><a href="#cite_note-sd9-56">[55]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canada" title="Atlantic Canada">Atlantic Canada</a> also experienced flooding, but to a much lesser degree.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> Overall, Floyd caused about $6.9 billion in damage and 73 fatalities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-floyd_tcr_61-3"><a href="#cite_note-floyd_tcr-61">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cw_65-2"><a href="#cite_note-cw-65">[64]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Gert">Hurricane Gert</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Hurricane Gert">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gert_09-15-1999_1715Z.png"><img alt="Gert 09-15-1999 1715Z.png" data-file-height="2287" data-file-width="2132" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Gert_09-15-1999_1715Z.png/150px-Gert_09-15-1999_1715Z.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Gert_09-15-1999_1715Z.png/225px-Gert_09-15-1999_1715Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Gert_09-15-1999_1715Z.png/300px-Gert_09-15-1999_1715Z.png 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gert_1999_track.png"><img alt="Gert 1999 track.png" data-file-height="883" data-file-width="1024" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Gert_1999_track.png/150px-Gert_1999_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Gert_1999_track.png/225px-Gert_1999_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Gert_1999_track.png/300px-Gert_1999_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 11 – September 23</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>150 mph (240 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  930 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gert_(1999)" title="Hurricane Gert (1999)">Hurricane Gert (1999)</a></div>
<p>On September 10, a tropical wave moved off the coast of Africa. Due to the development of a low-level circulation and convective banding, the wave became a tropical depression at 12:00 UTC on September 11 to the south of the Cape Verde islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gtcr_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-gtcr-68">[67]</a></sup> After increases in intensity, banding features, and outflow improvement,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> the depression was upgraded to Tropical Storm Gert on September 12 while moving west-northwestward to the south of a subtropical ridge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gtcr_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-gtcr-68">[67]</a></sup> Warm ocean temperatures and an anticyclone aloft allowed Gert to reach hurricane intensity by the following day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gtcr_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-gtcr-68">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> Early on September 15, Gert attained major hurricane strength. After reaching Category 4 status that day, Gert strengthened further, peaking with maximum sustained winds of 150 mph (240 km/h) and a minimum barometric pressure of 930 mbar (27 inHg) on September 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gtcr_68-3"><a href="#cite_note-gtcr-68">[67]</a></sup> An eyewall replacement cyclone, as well as increasing wind shear and an upper-level trough restricting outflow later on,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> Gert weakened to a low-end Category 3 on September 18.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gtcr_68-4"><a href="#cite_note-gtcr-68">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gert re-strengthened to a Category 4 hurricane on September 19.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gtcr_68-5"><a href="#cite_note-gtcr-68">[67]</a></sup> However, dry air and colder sea surface temperatures began causing the storm to weaken,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> with Gert falling to a Category 3 hurricane on September 20 and a Category 2 hurricane on September 21. That day, the hurricane passed about 135 mi (215 km) east of Bermuda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gtcr_68-6"><a href="#cite_note-gtcr-68">[67]</a></sup> Accelerating northeastward under the influence of an approaching trough,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> Gert weakened to a tropical storm on September 23 after convection decreased around the center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gtcr_68-7"><a href="#cite_note-gtcr-68">[67]</a></sup> By 12:00 UTC on September 23, convection diminished enough that the storm transitioned into an extratropical cyclone while situated about 55 mi (90 km) southeast of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Race" title="Cape Race">Cape Race</a>, Newfoundland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gtcr_68-8"><a href="#cite_note-gtcr-68">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> About six hours later, the remnants of Gert were absorbed by a larger extratropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gtcr_68-9"><a href="#cite_note-gtcr-68">[67]</a></sup> For several days, Gert threatened to strike Bermuda, prompting the evacuation of tourists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-news-78">[77]</a></sup> Although Gert's center did not make landfall, it passed a short distance east of the island,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gtcr_68-10"><a href="#cite_note-gtcr-68">[67]</a></sup> producing hurricane-force winds that left 11,000 people without power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> High waves swept two people out to sea at <a href="/wiki/Acadia_National_Park" title="Acadia National Park">Acadia National Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gtcr_68-11"><a href="#cite_note-gtcr-68">[67]</a></sup> Later, strong waves struck Newfoundland and left heavy marine damage, with about $1.9 million in damage done to a wharf along the Avalon Peninsula.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Harvey">Tropical Storm Harvey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Harvey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Harvey_09-20-1999_1740Z.png"><img alt="Harvey 09-20-1999 1740Z.png" data-file-height="2593" data-file-width="2275" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Harvey_09-20-1999_1740Z.png/150px-Harvey_09-20-1999_1740Z.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Harvey_09-20-1999_1740Z.png/225px-Harvey_09-20-1999_1740Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Harvey_09-20-1999_1740Z.png/300px-Harvey_09-20-1999_1740Z.png 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Harvey_1999_track.png"><img alt="Harvey 1999 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Harvey_1999_track.png/150px-Harvey_1999_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Harvey_1999_track.png/225px-Harvey_1999_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Harvey_1999_track.png/300px-Harvey_1999_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 19 – September 22</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>60 mph (95 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  995 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Harvey_(1999)" title="Tropical Storm Harvey (1999)">Tropical Storm Harvey (1999)</a></div>
<p>A tropical wave that emerged into the Atlantic from the west coast of Africa on September 4 reached the Gulf of Mexico by September 18. Following an increase in convection, the system became a tropical depression at 06:00 UTC on September 19. The depression initially tracked due northward and strengthened into Tropical Storm Harvey by early on September 20. Harvey gradually intensified further and 24 hours after the upgrade, the storm peaked with winds of 60 mph (95 km/h) and a minimum barometric pressure of 995 mbar (29.4 inHg). Thereafter, no significant change in intensity occurred before the storm made landfall in <a href="/wiki/Everglades_City,_Florida" title="Everglades City, Florida">Everglades City, Florida</a>, late on September 21. Harvey then accelerated across Florida and by early on September 22, merged with a developing extratropical low while located near <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bahama" title="Grand Bahama">Grand Bahama</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-htcr_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-htcr-81">[80]</a></sup> The remnants reached Atlantic Canada before dissipating on September 24.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ECH_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-ECH-82">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Florida, precipitation peaked at 10.24 in (260 mm) in <a href="/wiki/Naples,_Florida" title="Naples, Florida">Naples</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Florida_Rain_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-Florida_Rain-64">[63]</a></sup> As a result, at least 34 houses and businesses were flooded. There were sporadic reports of tropical storm-force winds throughout the state,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd9_56-4"><a href="#cite_note-sd9-56">[55]</a></sup> as well as two tornadoes, neither of which caused left severe impact. Damage estimates in Florida reached about $15 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-htcr_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-htcr-81">[80]</a></sup> Throughout the rest of the United States, impact was limited, confined to light rainfall in Georgia, North Carolina, and South Carolina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPCSE_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-WPCSE-83">[82]</a></sup> Heavy precipitation was reported in Atlantic Canada, with 11.89 in (302 mm) of rain falling in <a href="/wiki/Oxford,_Nova_Scotia" title="Oxford, Nova Scotia">Oxford, Nova Scotia</a>, making Harvey the wettest tropical cyclone or remnants on record in that country. Significant flooding, especially to roads and houses, was reported throughout Atlantic Canada, with damage totaling at least $7.6 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ECH_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-ECH-82">[81]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Eleven">Tropical Depression Eleven</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Eleven">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
