</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 4 – October 6</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>35 mph (55 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1002 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/October_1999_Mexico_floods" title="October 1999 Mexico floods">October 1999 Mexico floods</a></div>
<p>Until a westward moving tropical wave reached the western Caribbean Sea on September 30, minimal organization occurred. The system eventually emerged into the Gulf of Mexico and developed into Tropical Depression Eleven on October 4. Weak steering current caused the depression to drift slowly and erratically, with the depression initially heading southward, before curving northwest. A surface trough over the central and eastern Gulf of Mexico prevented significant strengthening. The depression remained below tropical storm intensity, attaining its peak intensity on October 5, with maximum sustained winds of 35 mph (55 km/h) and a minimum barometric pressure of 1,002 mbar (29.6 inHg).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11tcr_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-11tcr-84">[83]</a></sup> While approaching the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast_of_Mexico" title="Gulf Coast of Mexico">Gulf Coast of Mexico</a>, the depression was absorbed by the surface trough at 18:00 UTC on October 6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11tcr_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-11tcr-84">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>The depression and its remnants contributed significantly to an <a href="/wiki/October_1999_Mexico_floods" title="October 1999 Mexico floods">ongoing flood in Mexico</a>, bring up to 43.23 in (1,098 mm) of rain to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jalacingo,_Veracruz" title="Jalacingo, Veracruz">Jalacingo, Veracruz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> Throughout Mexico, 90,000 houses were damaged or destroyed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gom1018_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-gom1018-86">[85]</a></sup> leaving about 500,000 people homeless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gom1028b_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-gom1028b-87">[86]</a></sup> Flooding caused thousands of landslides and 39 rivers to overflow, leading to the destruction of bridges, houses,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coping_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-coping-88">[87]</a></sup> widespread crop fields,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxfam29_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-oxfam29-89">[88]</a></sup> schools,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-satori_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-satori-90">[89]</a></sup> and electrical networks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gom1013_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-gom1013-91">[90]</a></sup> Flooding also extended into Central America in late September through early October, causing $40 million (385 million pesos) in crop damage and 70 deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scf_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-scf-92">[91]</a></sup> However, impact by the depression itself cannot be distinguished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11tcr_84-2"><a href="#cite_note-11tcr-84">[83]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Twelve">Tropical Depression Twelve</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Twelve">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:12L_10-06-1999_1815Z.png"><img alt="12L 10-06-1999 1815Z.png" data-file-height="1986" data-file-width="1740" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/12L_10-06-1999_1815Z.png/150px-12L_10-06-1999_1815Z.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/12L_10-06-1999_1815Z.png/225px-12L_10-06-1999_1815Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/12L_10-06-1999_1815Z.png/300px-12L_10-06-1999_1815Z.png 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:12-L_1999_track.png"><img alt="12-L 1999 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/12-L_1999_track.png/150px-12-L_1999_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/12-L_1999_track.png/225px-12-L_1999_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/12-L_1999_track.png/300px-12-L_1999_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 6 – October 8</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>35 mph (55 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1007 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On September 30, a tropical wave emerged into the Atlantic Ocean from the west coast of Africa. It slowly began to organize during the next several days and by early on October 6, developed into Tropical Depression Twelve while located about 1,075 mi (1,730 km) east of <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12tcr_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-12tcr-15">[14]</a></sup> Due to an anticyclone, conditions appeared favorable for significant strengthening, with the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> predicting the depression to be at least a strong tropical storm by October 9.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> However, wind shear began undercutting the anticyclone,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> which prevented any significant intensification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12tcr_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-12tcr-15">[14]</a></sup> Later on October 6, the low-level circulation became exposed to the west of the deep convection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> The depression never re-organized and instead deteriorated in structure due to shearing. Despite a burst in convection on October 8,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> the depression dissipated at 18:00 UTC while located about 875 mi (1,410 km) east-northeast of <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12tcr_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-12tcr-15">[14]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Irene">Hurricane Irene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Hurricane Irene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Irene_10-18-1999_1531Z.png"><img alt="Irene 10-18-1999 1531Z.png" data-file-height="1194" data-file-width="1049" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Irene_10-18-1999_1531Z.png/150px-Irene_10-18-1999_1531Z.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Irene_10-18-1999_1531Z.png/225px-Irene_10-18-1999_1531Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Irene_10-18-1999_1531Z.png/300px-Irene_10-18-1999_1531Z.png 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Irene_1999_track.png"><img alt="Irene 1999 track.png" data-file-height="933" data-file-width="1024" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Irene_1999_track.png/150px-Irene_1999_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Irene_1999_track.png/225px-Irene_1999_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Irene_1999_track.png/300px-Irene_1999_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 12 – October 19</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>110 mph (175 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  960 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irene_(1999)" title="Hurricane Irene (1999)">Hurricane Irene (1999)</a></div>
<p>A broad trough of low pressure developed into a tropical depression while south of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isle_of_Youth" title="Isle of Youth">Isle of Youth</a> on October 12. It headed north and soon intensified into Tropical Storm Irene. On October 14, the storm passed over the Isle of Youth and western <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>. While over the <a href="/wiki/Straits_of_Florida" title="Straits of Florida">Straits of Florida</a>, Irene reached hurricane strength. The next day, it made landfall in <a href="/wiki/Key_West,_Florida" title="Key West, Florida">Key West, Florida</a>, and again near <a href="/wiki/Cape_Sable" title="Cape Sable">Cape Sable</a>. Later on October 15, Irene moved back over water near <a href="/wiki/Jupiter,_Florida" title="Jupiter, Florida">Jupiter</a> as a minimal hurricane. It slowly strengthened as it paralleled the East Coast of the United States. When Irene interacted with a trough from the west, while over the warm Gulf Stream waters, the hurricane rapidly intensified and attained its peak intensity with maximum sustained winds 110 mph (180 km/h) and a minimum barometric pressure of 960 mbar (28 inHg) on October 18. However, after accelerating northeast, Irene weakened over the cooler waters of the North Atlantic. On October 19, the hurricane transitioned into an extratropical cyclone near Newfoundland and was absorbed by an extratropical low shortly thereafter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-irene_tcr_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-irene_tcr-97">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>Irene dropped heavy rainfall throughout its path, especially in Cuba and Florida. Rainfall on Cuba peaked at 35.6 in (905 mm) in Manaca-Iznaga,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> while the rest of the island reported more than 7 in (178 mm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-irene_tcr_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-irene_tcr-97">[96]</a></sup> Flooding resulted from the heavy rains, damaging more than 27,000 homes and causing significant effects to banana plantations and sugar cane fields.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cubcrop_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-cubcrop-99">[98]</a></sup> Hurricane forces winds were also reported in <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-irene_tcr_97-2"><a href="#cite_note-irene_tcr-97">[96]</a></sup> Four fatalities were reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-100">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cubreport_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-cubreport-101">[100]</a></sup> The storm brought flooding to Florida, particularly the southern portion of the state, where 17.45 in (443 mm) of rain fell in <a href="/wiki/Boynton_Beach,_Florida" title="Boynton Beach, Florida">Boynton Beach</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Florida_Rain_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-Florida_Rain-64">[63]</a></sup> Hundreds were displaced from their homes and thousands were isolated. Five people died from walking through electrified water after a power line fell, while three others drowned after unintentionally driving their vehicle into a canal. Total damage in Florida was around $800 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-irene_tcr_97-3"><a href="#cite_note-irene_tcr-97">[96]</a></sup> The hurricane left five deaths in the Bahamas, one direct and four indirect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bahdam_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-bahdam-102">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnnkey_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnnkey-103">[102]</a></sup> Irene also contributed slightly to ongoing flood problems in North Carolina in the aftermath of Hurricane Floyd.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-irene_tcr_97-4"><a href="#cite_note-irene_tcr-97">[96]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Jose">Hurricane Jose</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Hurricane Jose">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jose_10-20-1999_1515Z.png"><img alt="Jose 10-20-1999 1515Z.png" data-file-height="3022" data-file-width="2609" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Jose_10-20-1999_1515Z.png/150px-Jose_10-20-1999_1515Z.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Jose_10-20-1999_1515Z.png/225px-Jose_10-20-1999_1515Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Jose_10-20-1999_1515Z.png/300px-Jose_10-20-1999_1515Z.png 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jose_1999_track.png"><img alt="Jose 1999 track.png" data-file-height="867" data-file-width="1024" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Jose_1999_track.png/150px-Jose_1999_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Jose_1999_track.png/225px-Jose_1999_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Jose_1999_track.png/300px-Jose_1999_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 17 – October 25</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>100 mph (155 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  979 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(1999)" title="Hurricane Jose (1999)">Hurricane Jose (1999)</a></div>
<p>A tropical wave entered the Atlantic on October 8 and developed into a tropical depression while located 700 mi (1,100 km) east of the Windward Islands on October 17. The depression strengthened and by early on October 18, it was upgraded to Tropical Storm Jose. Intensification continued as Jose tracked west-northwestward and Jose reached hurricane status late on October 19. The storm became a Category 2 hurricane, though unfavorable conditions weakened it back. Later on October 21, Jose began moving through the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> as a Category 1 and fell to tropical storm intensity before reentering the Atlantic later that day. While north of Puerto Rico on October 22, Jose re-curved northeastward. The storm eventually began to accelerate and re-strengthen, reaching hurricane status again on October 24. After twelve hours as a hurricane, colder sea surface temperatures weakened Jose to a tropical storm on October 25, shortly before it became extratropical.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jtcr_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-jtcr-104">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>The worst of the effects from Jose occurred in <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a>, as winds up to 102 mph (164 km/h) were reported. About 500 houses and a newly built church were destroyed. About 50% of residents were left without water and 90% of people experienced power outages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hurr99c_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-hurr99c-105">[104]</a></sup> Overall, twelve people were injured, one fatality occurred, and an elderly blind man was listed as missing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ifrc_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-ifrc-106">[105]</a></sup> Flooding in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis">Saint Kitts and Nevis</a> washed out several major roads and caused landslides. Additionally, one person was killed during the storm. In <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a>, mudslides and flooding damaged houses and roads, especially those in low-lying areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jtcr_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-jtcr-104">[103]</a></sup> Nearly 15 in (380 mm) of rain and winds up to 100 mph (160 km/h) in <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a> left roads impassable and power outages, and damaged houses, crops, and shipping facilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ifrc_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-ifrc-106">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> Strong winds and heavy rainfall in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">United States Virgin Islands</a> caused extensive power outages and minor damage, estimated at $40,000. Overall, losses from the storm was less than $5 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sd10_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-sd10-108">[107]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Katrina">Tropical Storm Katrina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Katrina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Katrina_10-29-1999_1915Z.png"><img alt="Katrina 10-29-1999 1915Z.png" data-file-height="3573" data-file-width="3268" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Katrina_10-29-1999_1915Z.png/150px-Katrina_10-29-1999_1915Z.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Katrina_10-29-1999_1915Z.png/225px-Katrina_10-29-1999_1915Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Katrina_10-29-1999_1915Z.png/300px-Katrina_10-29-1999_1915Z.png 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Katrina_1999_track.png"><img alt="Katrina 1999 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Katrina_1999_track.png/150px-Katrina_1999_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Katrina_1999_track.png/225px-Katrina_1999_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Katrina_1999_track.png/300px-Katrina_1999_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 28 – November 1</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>40 mph (65 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  999 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Katrina_(1999)" title="Tropical Storm Katrina (1999)">Tropical Storm Katrina (1999)</a></div>
<p>A broad area of low pressure associated with remnants of a cold front developed into Tropical Depression Fifteen in the southwestern Caribbean Sea on October 28. Twenty-four hours later, it strengthened into Tropical Storm Katrina. The storm made near landfall <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Cabezas" title="Puerto Cabezas">Puerto Cabezas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>, on October 30. Later that day, Katrina weakened back to a tropical depression. It continued northwestward across Nicaragua and <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a>, before reemerging into the Caribbean Sea off the coast of Honduras on October 31. However, Katrina did not re-intensify and moved inland over the Yucatán Peninsula later that day. While approaching the Gulf of Mexico, Katrina was absorbed by a cold front on November 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Katrina_TCR_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Katrina_TCR-109">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>Katrina dropped heavy rainfall across, which was reported between 10 and 15 in (250 to 375 mm) throughout Nicaragua and Honduras.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAANews_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAANews-110">[109]</a></sup> As a result of the flooding, roughly 1,200 people were evacuated to emergency shelters in Honduras. Flooding also damage five bridges in Honduras, and the cities of Tocoa and Trujillo were isolated as the <a href="/wiki/Agu%C3%A1n_River" title="Aguán River">Aguán</a> and Siline rivers overflowed their banks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OCHA1_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-OCHA1-111">[110]</a></sup> Katrina also destroyed water pipes that were replaced shortly after destruction from Hurricane Mitch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> Shortly before dissipating, Katrina dropped moderate rainfall across the Yucatán Peninsula and eastern Mexico, peaking at 6.32 in (161 mm) in <a href="/wiki/Cunduac%C3%A1n" title="Cunduacán">Cunduacán</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPCMAX_25-4"><a href="#cite_note-WPCMAX-25">[24]</a></sup> Six years later, the name Katrina was used again <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">in 2005 for a hurricane</a> that devastated the Gulf Coast of the United States, particularly coastal <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">Mississippi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mwr2005_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-mwr2005-17">[16]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Lenny">Hurricane Lenny</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Hurricane Lenny">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">

<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>November 13 – November 23</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>155 mph (250 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  933 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lenny" title="Hurricane Lenny">Hurricane Lenny</a></div>
<p>A low pressure area developed into a tropical depression about 175 mi (280 km) south of the Cayman Islands at 18:00 UTC on November 13. The depression began to move in an unusual eastward track across the Caribbean Sea along the southern periphery of a trough and strengthened into Tropical Storm Lenny on the following day. It attained hurricane status south of Jamaica on November 15 and passed south of Hispaniola and Puerto Rico over the next few days. Beginning on November 16, Lenny underwent rapid deepening, becoming a major hurricane early on November 17 while south of the <a href="/wiki/Mona_Passage" title="Mona Passage">Mona Passage</a>. Later that day, Lenny peaked as a Category 4 hurricane with winds of 155 mph (250 km/h) and a minimum pressure of 933 mbar (27.6 inHg) while near Saint Croix. It gradually weakened due to wind shear while moving through the Leeward Islands, where it struck <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Barth%C3%A9lemy" title="Saint Barthélemy">Saint Barthélemy</a>. The system weakened to a tropical storm on November 19. After clearing the islands, Lenny deteriorated to a tropical depression on November 21 and dissipated on November 23, while located about 690 mi (1,110 km) east of the Lesser Antilles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ltcr_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-ltcr-18">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before moving through the Lesser Antilles, Lenny produced rough surf that killed two people in northern Colombia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ltcr_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-ltcr-18">[17]</a></sup> Strong winds and rainfall resulted in heavy crop damage in southeastern Puerto Rico. Lenny brought more heavy rains to areas in the Leeward Islands that had been affected by Hurricane Jose just one month earlier, and brought more damage to areas struck by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Georges" title="Hurricane Georges">Hurricane Georges</a> in 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-srh_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-srh-113">[112]</a></sup> Despite the hurricane's passage near Saint Croix at peak intensity,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ltcr_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-ltcr-18">[17]</a></sup> damage on the small island was only described as "moderate", although there was widespread flooding and erosion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ltcr_18-4"><a href="#cite_note-ltcr-18">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-srh_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-srh-113">[112]</a></sup> Damage in the United States territories totaled about $330 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ltcr_18-5"><a href="#cite_note-ltcr-18">[17]</a></sup> The highest precipitation total was 34.12 in (867 mm) at the police station on the French side of Saint Martin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPCMAX_25-5"><a href="#cite_note-WPCMAX-25">[24]</a></sup> On the island, the hurricane killed three people and destroyed more than 200 properties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ltcr_18-6"><a href="#cite_note-ltcr-18">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ifrc1122_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-ifrc1122-114">[113]</a></sup> In nearby Antigua and Barbuda, the hurricane killed one person;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usaid_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-usaid-115">[114]</a></sup> torrential rainfall there contaminated the local water supply. Significant storm damage occurred as far south as Grenada, where high surf isolated towns from the capital city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lennyspo_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-lennyspo-116">[115]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Storm_names">Storm names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Storm names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Atlantic_hurricane_names" title="List of retired Atlantic hurricane names">List of retired Atlantic hurricane names</a></div>
<p>The following names were used during the 1999 Atlantic hurricane season in North Atlantic for systems that reached at least tropical storm intensity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> It is the same list used for the <a href="/wiki/1993_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1993 Atlantic hurricane season">1993 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> A storm was named Lenny for the first (and only) time in 1999. The <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> retired the names Floyd and Lenny in the spring of 2000 and replaced them with Franklin and Lee for use in the <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005 season</a>. All of the remaining names were re-used in the 2005 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> Names that were not assigned are marked in <span style="color:#666666">gray</span>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_effects">Season effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Season effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This is a table of the storms in 1999 and their landfall(s), if any. Deaths in parentheses are additional and indirect (an example of an indirect death would be a traffic accident), but are still storm-related. Damage and deaths include totals while the storm was extratropical or a wave or low.</p>
